8.1 මූල්‍ය ප්‍රතිඵල

මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශනය අනුව 2016 දෙසැම්බර්‌ 31 දිනෙන්‌ අවසන්‌ වර්ෂය

යුතුවේ.

(අ) සහාධිපත්‍ය දෝපල කළමනාකරණය      කළමනාකරණ සංස්ථා අධික්ෂණය විධිමත්‌ නොවීම.

සහාධිපත්‍ය දෝපලවල පොදු පහසුකම්‌ පැටරීමේ කටයුතු
කඩිනම්‌ කිරීමට කටයුතු නොකිරීම.
- අනවසර ඉදිකිරීම සම්බන්ධ චාර්තා පවත්වා නොතිබීම.

(ආ) ලේඛන පවත්වා ගැනීම                  - බඩුූ චට්ටෝරු පොත්‌ පවන්චා නොතිබීම
- දුරකථන, ජලය, විදුලිය හා ඉන්ධන වියදම්‌ පාලනය
සඳහා ලේඛන පවත්වා නොතිබීම.

(අ) මූල්‍ය පාලනය               - වියිමන්‌ ආකෘතියකින්‌ ගා පාලනයකින්‌ නොරව අගිම
ඉල්ලුම්‌ කිරිම ගා වියදම්‌ කිරීම.

(අ වාහන පාලනය           - වාහන වලට අදාල ධාවන සටහන්‌ විධිමන්‌ ලෙස
පවත්වා නොතිබීම හා ටිගණකාධිපති වෙත යොමුකර
නොතිබීම.

- වටිනාකම වාර්ෂිකව තක්සේරු කිරීමකින්‌ තනොරව

වාහන රක්ෂණය කර තිබිම.

එච්‌.එම්‌. ගාම්‌ි     ජ්සිංහ

මූලෟ ප්‍රකාශය

ගිණුම පළබල සටහන්‌
01. ගිණුම්‌ පිළිබඳ සටහන්‌

පොදුවේ පිළිගත්‌ ගිණුම මූලධර්ම වලට අනුකූලව රාජ්‍ය අංශයේ ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රමිත කමිටුවේ අනුමත කරන ලද
ශිලංකා රාජ්‍ය අංශ ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රමිත තෝරා ගැනීම තුලින්‌ අවස්ථානෝචිත පරිද සාධාරණ ලෙස ගිණුම්කරණ
ඇස්තමේන්තු සකස්‌ කරමින්‌ මෙම ගිණුම්‌ ප්‍රකාශ ඉදිරිපත්‌ කර ඇත.

වංචා හෝ වැරදි හේතුවෙන්‌ ඇති විය හැකි ප්‍රමාණාත්මක සාවද්‍ය ප්‍රකාශයන්ගෙන්‌ තොරව මනා අභ්‍යන්තර
පාලනයක්‌ සැළසුම්‌ කිරීම සහ එය කියාත්මක කිරීමට හා පවත්වාගෙන යාම තුළින්‌ සාධාරණ ලෙස මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශන
ඉදිරිපත්‌ කිරීමට කටයුතු කර ඇති බවට සහතික වෙමු.

02.ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රතිපත්ති

පිළිගත්‌ ගිණුම්කරණ ප්‍රතිපත්තීන්ට අනුකුලව අනන්‍ය වශයෙන්‌ කාලපරිච්ඡේද පිළිබඳ අන්තර්‌ සම්බන්ධතාවයකින්‌
යුක්තව එෙතිහාසික අය පදනම්‌ මත අධිකාරියේ ගිණුම්‌ වාර්තා ඉදිරිපත්‌ කර ඇති මූල්‍ය ප්‍රතිපත්ති වලට බලපෑ
හැකි උද්ධමනකාරි සාධක අරභයා ගැලපුම්‌ කිරීමක්‌ කර නැති අතර උපචිත පදනම්‌ මත වාර්තා සකස්‌ කර ඇත.

3.සහායධිපත්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අධිකාරිය , කොළඹ - 02 , ශී චිත්තම්පලම ඒ ගාඩනර්‌ මාවත , ජාතික නිවාස
දෙපාර්තමේන්තු ගොඩනැගිල්ලේ පිහිටා ඇති අතර මුළු දවයිනටම අදාල වන පරිද සහාධිපත්‍ය දේපළ සම්බන්ධ
නියාමන කාර්යයන්‌ ඉටුකරනු ලබයි.

04.අධිකාරියේ නෛතික ස්වභාවය

පහසුකම්‌ පලදරන්නන්ගේ අවශ්‍යතාවයන්‌ සපිරෙන පරිදි ලබා ඇති බවට සහතික කිරීමත්‌ සිදුකරනු ලබයි.

කර ඇත. ඒ අනුව වාර්ෂික ක්ෂය වටිනාකම වශයෙන්‌ රැ :4,069,960 ක්‌ ප්‍රවර්ථන වර්ෂයේ ලාභයට ගැලපීමටද
කටයුතු කරන ලදි.

එමෙන්ම පසුගිය වර්ෂයේ ගැළපුම්‌ හේතුවෙන්‌ යන්ත්‍ර හා උපකරණ සඳහා වාර්ෂික ක්ෂය වටිනාකමින්‌ රු: 88,980.80
සහ කාර්යාල ලී බඩු සහ උපාංග සඳහා වාර්ෂික ක්ෂය වටිනාකමින්‌ රු : 98,926ක්ද අඩු කිරීමක්‌ හේතුවෙන්‌ සටහන්‌

නගමු පුරවර 2015 වර්ෂයේ ව්‍යාපෘති

එවියුඩි/ඒ /'සීළම්ජ්‌/1/1 6/07                                         2017 දෙසැම්බර්‌ 21 දින

සභාපති.

සහාධිපත්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අධිකාරිය.

සහාධිපත්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අධිකාරියේ 2016 දෙසැම්බර්‌ 31 දිනෙන්‌ අවසන්‌ වර්ෂය සඳහා වූ මූල්‍ය
ප්‍රකාශන පිළිබඳව 1071 අංක 38 දරන මුදල්‌ පනතේ 14(2)(සී) වගන්තිය ප්‍රකාර විගණකාධිපති වාර්තාව

මාගේ සමාංක හා 2017 සැප්තැම්බර්‌ 12 දිනැති ලිපියට යොමුවේ.

02. ඉහත සඳහන්‌ ලිපිය සමඟ එවන ලද මාගේ වාර්තාවේ දෙමළ අනුවාදය මේ සමහ එවා ඇත.

Dhiectives oi the
Authority

es ——

Control, manage, maintain and administer the
Condominium parcels, the Common elements
and the common amenities of the Condominium
Property or Semi Condominium Property;

Ensure the common elements and the Common
Amenities of the Condominium Property or Semi
Condominium Property are properly maintained
in good order and that periodic repairs are being
Carried out in order to maintain such property
in good and serviceable order, and to assist the
management corporation or the owner or owners
or occupiers to Carry out such activities in the event
of the management corporation or owner or owners
or occupiers failing to carry out such activities;

Ensure that all buildings comprising such
Condominium parcels are insured against risk of fire,
civil commotion and riot or to insure or keep insured,
if so requested by the management corporation
or by the owners, and to recover such premium or
Charges from the management corporation or the
owners as the case may be;

Remove all such unauthorized constructions erected
or carried out by the respective owners or occupiers
of such Condominium Parcels or by any person,
Contrary to the registered Condominium Plan of
the Condominium Property or the registered Semi
Condominium Property;

Ensure that the management corporation of the
Condominium Property or Semi Condominium
Property are properly functioning and to manage
and administer the activities of such management
Corporation;

Assist the management corporation or the owner or
owners or occupiers of the Condominium Parcels, of
the Condominium Property or Semi Condominium
Property in providing the services such as water,
Sewerage, drainage, gas, electricity, garbage disposal,
air conditioning, telephone, radio and redifussion
Services to the owner or owners or occupiers of
the Condominium Parcels of such Condominium
Property or Semi Condominium Property;

Assist the management corporation to establish
and maintain for use by owners or occupiers of
Such condominium parcels , facilities such as roads
, access ways , lawns , gardens , parks , play grounds
and other open spaces , or to be directly involved
with such activities in the event of the management
Corporation failing to establish and maintain such
facilities

Transfer to the local authority the maintenance
of roads, access ways, lawns, gardens, parks,
playgrounds, and other open spaces for the use by
owners or occupiers of the Condominium Parcels of
the Condominium Property or Semi Condominium
Property;

Provide maintenance and repair services to such
Condominium Parcels of the Condominium Property
or Semi Condominium property at the request of
the management corporation or owners or occupiers
thereof;

Monitor the progress of the construction of the
registered provisional Condominium Property in
order to ensure that the interests of the stakeholders
are protected and to intervene wherever necessary
to protect such interests;

Formulate and submit Condominium re-
development program including capital investment
plans to the Minister for approval by the Government

Li

Call upon the National Housing Development
Authority or the Urban Development Authority
or any local authority or any government agency
or any private sector developer, to undertake
the implementation of such Condominium re-
development projects, or to undertake the
execution of the Condominium re-development
projects, of such program as may be approved by
the Government;

Undertake the completion of any Condominium
Building shown in the registered Semi Condominium
Plan or Provisional Condominium Plan , in the event
of any owner failing to complete such project;

Develop or re-develop land for carrying out of any of
the objectives of the Authority and

Do all such other acts as may be necessary or
conducive to the attainment of any or all of the
above objectives.

Report of the Administrative

In the year 2016, an income of Rs. 197.254 million
was generated through the operational activities
of the Authority and with the receipt of a treasury
provision of Rs 1 million as recurrent expenditure
for the payment of salaries of employees, the overall
income stood at Rs. 108.254 million. In comparison to
operational income in the year 2015 which amounted
to Rs. 125.75 million, the operational income has
posted a growth of 63.41%. The overall expenditurein
the year 2015 was Rs. 97.4 million and in comparison,
the overall expenditure in 2016 was Rs.109.44 million.
The net post tax profit in year 2016 was Rs 70.41
million and significantly this was the highest profit
recorded during the period from year 2003 to date.

This increase in the income can be attributable to
the following factors prevailed in the condominium
property sector.

© Notable increase in the Construction of new
Condominium properties

© increase in the Construction of Condominium
properties by both the state and private sectors from
year 2015.

© Arrival of foreign investors for the construction of
large scale mix condominium properties in Colombo
City.

Issuance of initial clearance for the
construction of condominium properties

With a view to minimizing recurrent problems such as
the furnishing the condominium plan to the Authority
after the construction of the condominium property
and inadequate provision of common amenities in
Certain constructions, it has been decided that inital
Clearance instructions should be sought from this
Authority. Accordingly, initial clearance was granted
to 106 Condominium properties proposed to be
Constructed in 2015 and 205 clearance letters were
issued in 2016. These clearance instructions served as
guidance to property developers in the construction
activities.

Issuance of Condominium Certificates

One of the key regulatory responsibilities of this
Authority is to ensure that Common amenities and
Common elements are available in the condominium
properties constructed by the public or private sector
for the benefit and welfare of the residents. As a
result of these condominium Certificates, the unit
owners of the property have undisturbed possession
of the common amenities and Common elements.
The certificates have also contributed to prevent the
registration of property on forged documents and the
delay in disposing the ownership after having obtained
money through sales agreement.

Further, the issuance of this certificate has assured
the conformity with construction standards, proper
provision of utilities such as insurance schemes, water,
and electricity while also making it possible to exert
pressure on the property developer for the provision
of such facilities.

The income generated through the issuance of
Condominium certificates is the main source of income
of the Authority. From 2005, the Authority has issued
1115 such certificates. It was planned to issue 102
Certificates in the year 2016 and the Authority was
able to reach the target by the end of the year.

Accordingly, details of Certificates issued by the
Authority during the period from 2014 to 2016 are
tabulated below.

Annual      Progress
targets
Imancial            20.425          04.160
2014      (Rs. Mn)
Physical          75           110
Financial            67.242          18.30

Physical                     102                     102

Of the applications forwarded in the year 2016 seeking
to obtain Condominium certificates, certificates were
not issued in respect of 04 of them owing to the non
issue of Certificate of compliance, not granting deeds
and other shortcomings.

AN new trend in the construction of condominium
property has emerged with then entry o foreign
investors into the condominium sector in 2014.

An increasing trend in the construction of properties is
witnessed also due to the construction of condominium
properties by the Urban Development Authority for
resettling tenement settlers and the construction of
500,000 houses under the new programme of the
government.

Nearly 80 buildings constructed by the private
sector are unable to apply for the certification of
the Authority on account of being unable to obtain
Certificates of Compliance. There are 63 such
properties of the National Housing Development
Authority as well. In order to address this issue, the
Authority as the regulator of the sector, has obtained
the approval of the Cabinet of Ministers to amend
the Apartment Ownership Act No 04 of 1999 and the
relevant amendments have been referred to the Legal
Draughtsman and the relevant draft bill is now under
examination.

Report of the Administrative

As per Apartment Ownership Act No 11 of 1973, itisnot
mandatory to register a condominium plan. Therefore,
new amendments have been proposed making it
mandatory for the registration of all condominium
plans and a report to that effect has been referred to
the Legal Draftsman for necessary action.

Establishing, registering and actively
maintaining Management Corporations

Though apropertywith private ownershipis maintained
by the owners of such property, the maintenance
of Common elements and common amenities in a
Condominium property with shared ownership cannot
be maintained by any single individual and as such all
those who share these commonelements and common
amenities band together to constitute management
Corporations which are the legal structure for their
administration.

From the year 2005 up to now, the authority has
constituted management Corporations in 927
Condominium properties.

The progress achieved in establishing Management
Corporations by the Authority from 2014 up to 2016 is
Summarized in the following table.

mittees/ renewal of registration /reactivating dor-

However, the following difficulties were experienced in
establishing management corporations

€e lack of understanding among property owners
regarding the importance of the Management
Corporation for maintaining property

© Lack of interest among residents of the apartment
housing schemes Constructed by the government
agencies such as the Urban Development Authority
for the establishment of management corporations

€ Owners of condominium property constructed by
the private sector not residing permanently in them

© Lassitude of owners to be involved in maintenance
and management acuavities under a voluntary basis
que to them being busy.

© Defaulting the payment of maintenance fees and
other residents not cooperating with the panel of
office bearers of the Management Corporation.

€ Objections raised by the majority of occupants over
the high prevalence of unauthorized structures
in condominium properties Constructed by the
government.

Resolving disputes of Condominium
Property

The Authority has been vested with powers Common
Amenities Board Law No 10 of 1073 to intervene inthe
event of disputes arising between the management of
the condominium property and the property owner or
between the residents and the owner or between the
owner and the buyer. Accordingly, when a complaint
is forwarded to the Authority in writing by those who
have entered into a sales agreement to purchase
Condominium property or a resident, the Authority
initiates necessary action for its prompt resolution.
Dispute which cannot be resolved are referred to an
investigation.

An investigation Council has been set up for the
resolution of such disputes. The complaints received
by the Council can be categorized as follows according
to their nature.

©Not Granting deeds to the residents since the
Condominium Plan Cannot be registered despite the
lapse of a long period of time since the construction
and sale through a sales agreement.

€ Construction in violation of the approved building
plan; some property developers are unable to obtain
the certificate of compliance as they have executed
sales agreement after constructing only several
floors.

© Not providing Common amenities and Common
elements in accordance with the approved plan

© Residents not paying the monthly maintenance fee
to the Management Corporation

© reciting unauthorized structures and problems
arising in using Car parks and the public areas

In the year 2016, the Authority has taken measures to
resolve 65 complaints so received.

No of disputes resolved
2014                              75
2015                              60
2016                              605

Awareness Programmes

Educating Management Corporations, which is the
legal structure of residents of condominium property
as provided for by the Apartment Ownership Act
No. 11 of 1073 and the Common Amenities Board
Law No. 10 of 1973 and creating awareness among
property developers and other stakeholders on the
administration and maintenance of the property has
to be carried out on a regular basis.

Creating awareness among all stakeholders of the
Condominium property is continually Carried through
following steps.

e Distributing 10,000 Copies of “Condominium”
leaflets.
ee Printing and distributing 3,000 Condominium

handbooks authored by the Chairman.

© Conducting the annual general meetings and special
general meetings of Management Corporations
under the patronage of the officials of the Authority

Transferring Ownership of Tsunami
property constructed under Tsunami
rehabilitation

The following facts came to light during the survey
Conducted by the Authority on condominium property
Constructed under Tsunami rehabilitation.

€ The number of housing schemes constructed as flats
is 39 and the number of housing units is 3749.

© The number of houses schemes constructed as twin
houses (joint) is 30 and the number of housing units
is 2064.

The Authority, having taken into account the fact
that no measures had been taken to dispose of the
ownership of these housing schemes, took this matter
up with the Ministry of Land and Land Development

which owns these lands and as a result such
negotiations the approval of the Cabinet of Ministers
was Secured to introduce amendments to the Land Act
to enable the transfer of ownership of such lands and
the drafting of relevant regulations has been finalized
by now and action has been initiated to refer same to
the Legal Draftsman’s Department.

For this purpose, the Authority Conducted 02
workshops in partnership with the Ministry of Land,
the Land Department and the Survey Department and
the draft of the necessary regulations was formulated.
Action is also being pursued in collaboration with the
District Secretary, Matara to award deeds in respect of
two apartment housing schemes inthe Matara district.

Renovation of multi storeyed housing
schemes of government

The following multi-storied housing schemes were
renovated in year 2016 using unspent treasury funds
for the work continued from 2015.

© [unawa Samudra Shakthihousing scheme
© Hilda Flats housing scheme, Dehiwala
© Alokapura housing scheme, Hambantota

In addition, Rs 35.802 million allocated by the treasury
was Spent on the special project for rehabilitating rain
water drainage system and Carpeting roads of the
following 03 housing schemes in 2016.

© Jaltharahousing scheme
© NMattergoda housing scheme

© Kindawatta housing scheme

Regulatory interventions of Condominium
Management Authority

Employing the aforementioned powers and provisions,
the Condominium Management Authority has been
able to execute the following very important services
during the year 2016.

© Measures were taken in the year 2015 to seek the
approval of the Cabinet to amend the Apartment
Ownership (Special Provisions) Act No 04 of 1904
enabling the registration of properties which had
been Constructed several decades ago but which
have not been registered as a condominium property
thus preventing the handing over of their ownership
to the residents. The relevant draft which will enable
to the granting of deeds is in the process of being
drafted by the Legal Draftsman. More than 15,000
families of housing schemes constructed by the
public and private sectors who have not been ableto
Secure deeds for their houses for more than 30-40
years will be benefited from this programme.

Report of the Administrative

€ The panel of experts appointed by the Cabinet of
Ministers to make amendments to the Common
Amenities Law No. 10 of 1973 and Apartment
Ownership Act No. 11 of 1973 has by now suggested
all the necessary amendments and same was
referred to the Legal Draftsman. The amended
bill will address most of the practical issues in the
Condominium sector and enable the Authority to
offer a wider range of services.

© Repulations made under the Condominium
Management Authority Law and the Apartment
Ownership Act were published in Gazette
Extraordinary No 2026/25 dated 05 July 2017. It
should be noted that this gazette notification could
only be issued nearly 10years after the establishment
of this Authority.

Restructuring Cadre

The cadre estimate and the promotion and recruitment
procedure of the Authority were approved by the
Department of Management Services in the year 2010.

Though the approved cadre of the Authority is 139,
the number of staff members by December 2016 was
102. Action will be taken in 2017 to fill the existing
vacancies.

Audit Report

[Neils {cTelelai                                                              Answer of the Authority

1.2 Management's Responsibility regarding the Financial Statements

The preparation and fair presentation of these financial statements

in accordance with Sri Lanka Accounting Standards for public sector
and deciding internal controls to enable the preparation of financial
Statements free from material misstatements whether due to error or
fraud is the responsibility of the management.

1.3 Responsibility Of the Auditor

My responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial
Statements based on my audit. | conducted my audit in accordance
with Sri Lanka auditing Standards corresponding to international audit
Standards of supreme audit institutions. (ISSA! 1000-1810) Those
Standards require that the audit is planned and performed to secure a
reasonable assurance whether the financial statements are free from
material misstatements. and disclosures in the financial statements.
The procedures selected depend on the auditor's judgment, including
the assessment of the risk of the material misstatement of the
Consolidated financial statements, whether due to fraud or error. In
making those risk assessments, the auditor considers internal control
relevant to the Authority's preparation and fair presentation of the
Consolidated financial statements in order to design audit procedures
that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose

of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Authority's
internal control. An audit also includes evaluating the appropriateness
of Accounting Policies used and the reasonableness of accounting
estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall
presentation of the financial statements. Sub section (3) and (4)

lam of the opinion that except for the effects on the financial

22     Comments on Financial Statements

2.4.1 Srilanka Public Sector Accounting Standards

The following observations are made.

(a) Srilanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 02

Adjustments of Rs. 650,41 and Rs 187,907 made in the Changes

of Equity Statement for gratuity and depreciation respectively for
the year 2015 had been adjusted for operational activities in the
Cash Flow Statement of the year under review and a previous year
adjustment value totaling Rs 1,130,822 had been adjusted to Cash
Flow Statement on financial activities of the year under review.

Will be corrected in the year 2017.

(hb) Srilanka Public Sector Accounting Standards 07

Though the useful life of an asset should be reviewed of each year and
treated as a change of the accounting estimate and the depreciable
period of time should be reviewed as at the last day of the reporting
period, the standard had not been complied with in respect of

assets totaling Rs 20.89 million of which the depreciation had been
Completed by the Authority and which are currently in use.

Action will be taken in the coming
year to revalue the assets and adjust
accounts.

(c) Srilanka Public Sector Accounting Standards 07

Though inventories should be measured at the lower of cost and
net realizable value, the Authority had formulated a policy regarding
inventories without complying with this and inventories had been
measured at the cost without measuring neat realizable value.

In the year 2017, shortcomings will
be corrected and stocks will be valued
as per the instructions of Accounting
Standard 9.

2.4.2 Accounting deficiencies

The following deficiencies were observed

(a) Since the office rent paid off in the year 2016 had beenthe
Office Rent Account and Accrued Office Rent Account had been
overestimated by Rs. 115,802.

Corrected through journal 109

(b) Action had not been taken to pay or account under current
liabilities during the year under review, a gratuity of Rs 315,418
allocated for an officer retired in the year 2016.

Action will be taken to correct this
when final accounts are prepared in
the year 2017.

2.23 Lack of evidence for audit

The Authority had not prepared journal vouchers for adjustments
amounting to Rs 262.99 million in preparing final accounts.

Action will be taken in the year 2017 to
prepare al journal vouchers

d Financial Review

d.1 Financial results

As per the financial statements, the surplus of the Authority for the
year ended 31 December 2016 was Rs. 70.41 million as against the
financial surplus of Rs.2 1.97 of the previous year. Thus a growth of Rs.
48.44 million was observed Though there was a reduction of Rs 11
million in the Treasury receipts for the payment of salaries when the
year under review is compared with the previous year, this growth can
mainly be attributable to the increase in operational expenditure by
Rs. 76.8 million.

In analyzing the financial outcome during the year under review and
the four preceding years, though a financial deficiency was shown in
the year 2013 a financial surplus has been recorded in other years.
The contribution of the institution has shown a growth from 2012
to 2016 after making adjustments for employee remuneration, taxes
paid to the government and the depreciation of non- current assets
and compared to previous year, the growth during the year under
review was 53%.

The upward revision of certificate fees
by a significant percentage after eight
years as per the board paper No. 07/16
submitted to 106th board meeting
held on 01.02.2016 and the decision to
levy 255 of the certificate fee in issuing
Clearance certificates as per board
paper No. 18/16 submitted to 100th
board meeting held on 08.07.2016
resulted in a substantial increase in

the condominium certificate income

in 2016. This was the key factor for the
growth of overall contribution by 53%
in the year 2016.

3.2 Analytical Financial Review

The following observations are made.

(a) The operational income during the year under review had
grown by Rs 76.8 million, i.e. by 72% on the back of the increase of
Condominium certificate income by Rs 83.66 million, i.e. by 107%
Compared to previous year. Further, due to the increase of interest
income for fixed deposits, the non-operational income had grown by
Rs 6.16 million or by 120% compared to preceding year.

The reasons attributed in paragraph
3.1 above to the increase in financial
result also directly impacted onthe
growth of certificate issuance income
and interest income.

(bh) As atthe end of the year under review, the net assets of the
Authority stood at Rs 102.79 million and conversely the net assets of
the previous year was Rs. 33.51 million. Thus an increase of Rs 69.28
million was observed in the net assets in comparison to previous year.
The gain of a surplus of Rs 70.41 million during the year under review
was largely responsible for the above growth.

The increase of the operational
income of the Authority on the basis
of reasons assigned for the increase in
financial result has had a direct impact
on growth of net assets by Rs 69.28
million.

(C)     As at the close of the year under review, the current asset
ratio was 1.7.1 and last year that ratio was 1.2.1. Similarly, the instant
assets ratio was 1.6.1 in the year under review and inthe year 2015,
that ratio was 1.2.1.

Due to the growth in the financial
result consequent to the impact of
above situations, the current ratio is
on the increase and the situation will
further improve in the coming years.

1. Operational Review

li Performance

(a)As per the Common Amenities Board Act No. 10 of 10973, the

main objective of the Authority is the management, maintenance

and control of common amenities of condominium properties and
offering guidance and assisting the management corporation for

the proper execution of same and making direct interventions when
maintenance is neglected. The disclosures from the audit in respect of
the performance of the Authority are given below.

25 Page



Audit Report

[Neils {cTelelai                                                              Answer of the Authority

(a) As per the Action Plan of the year under review andthe
progress review report of 31 December 2016, though it was targeted
to register 75 management corporations, only 33 had been registered,
hence the progress was 44%.

Awareness programmes for
management corporations are in
progress in 2017 using provisions
received from Treasury. Accordingly,
it will be possible to overcome this
Situation.

(b) Though it was planned to recover from the relevant parties, the
expenditure incurred on taking action to remove and for the removal
of 75 unauthorized structures in the year 2016, after identifying and
Conducting inspections on such structures and making the owners
aware and giving them reasonable me in the year 2016, the actual
number of unauthorized structures removed in the year was just

05. Similarly, though it it had been planned to take action to identity
unauthorized structures, the relevant Census report had not been
prepared even by the end of the year under review.

Census activities are being Carried
out and removal of unauthorized
Structures regarding which final
decision had been given after

the conduct of inspections too is
underway.

(Cc)     Though it had been planned to persuade management
Corporations to insure 80 condominium properties, only 56 properties
had been insured during the year under review and the management
had not paid attention on insuring remaining properties. Further,

as per the Action Plan of 2017, it had been planned to insure 160
Condominium properties.

The insuring of condominium
properties is an ongoing process.
However since the government built
Condominium properties are in a state
of disrepair, insuring them has become
problematic.

(dq) Though it had been planned to grant condominium property
registration certificates on a provision of Rs 10 million for 112
Condominium properties constructed for Tsunami affected people, the
Authority had failed to issue even a single Certificate during the year
under review.

The ownership of these lands on which
these properties are located lies with
Divisional Secretary and a situation has
arisen where certificate of conformity
Cannot be obtained for these
properties. However, inthe year 2017,
Condominium certificates were issued
in respect of two Tsunami properties
belonged to the National Housing
Development Authority and Hilda Flats
Housing Scheme.

(6)     Even though it had been planned as per the Action Plan of
2015 to amend the Apartment Ownership Act No 11 of 1973 under
five phases, i.e. conducting expert panel discussions, finalizing the
amended draft report, submitting for cabinet approval, publishing in
the gazette, presenting for the approval of Parliament and to complete
the entire process by November 2015, no one of these tasks had been
implemented. Therefore it had been planned again to complete the
aforesaid process by November 2016 in line with the Action Plan of
2016, but even by the end of the year under review, only the expert
Committee had been appointed and it had only held one meeting in
December 2016.

Reports of the panel of experts had
been referred to the Legal Draftsman'’s
Department.

(      Get together of targeted management corporation
representatives, awareness workshop for Divisional Secretaries of
Colombo district, workshop for creating awareness amongst local
government members of Colombo district and property developers
meeting had not been held during the year under review as per the
Action Plan of the Authority.

Action is being pursued to conduct
awareness programmes as planned in
the year 2017.

ll2 Management Activities

Payments amounting to Rs. 2.02 million had been paid in the year
1999 to a private company to purchase 750 items from 02 types of
goods required for the Authority and the Authority had received 545
items valued at Rs 1.22 million in the year 2002. As the remaining
items were not received, the Authority filed a case in 2006, but even
by the close of the year under review, the Authority had not taken
action to recover the dues as per the judgment delivered by the court.

These items had been ordered from
Lanka Net Company and the Company
had failed to supply goods to the value
of Rs. 807,187.

The Authority filed a case through
the Attorney General's Department to
recover this amount.

Further, it had been reported that

a Court ruling had been delivered
ordering the Department of Buildings
to settle an amount payable to Lanka
Net Limited.

The Chairman of Lanka Net Limited
notified in writing on 23.04.2003

that it would settle the amount of Rs
807,187 payable to this Authority upon
the receipt of the above sum.

recover this amount.

13 Onerational activities

The following observations are made.

(a) Though the Authority should actively maintain management
Corporations of condominium properties in terms of Condominium
Management Authority Act No 10 of 1973, only 427 out of 872
management corporations. i.e. 49% established by the Authority
remained inactive at the end of the year under review.

Programmes for creating awareness
amongst management corporations
are being conducted in 2017 using
provisions made available by the
Treasury.

(bh) Though it had been decided to launch a book titled
“Condominium Livino Emeroino Trend’ written by the Chairman of
the Authority consequent to a decision taken at the 108th meeting
of the management committee held on 25 May 2016 and to bear the

the Authority had instead printed an English medium book titled
“Condominium Living —Emerging Trend” at a cost of Rs 1.67 million.

printing costs.

Of the sum of Rs 562,273/- tobe

recovered as of now and action is
being taken to recover the remaining
amount of Rs 85,373/- swiftly.

un Underutilization of funds

The Chairman,

Condominium Management Authority

Report of the Auditor General on the Financial Statements of the Condominium
Management Authority for the year ended 31 December 2016 in terms of Section 14(2)(¢)
of the Finance Act No. 33 of 1971.

Ib        The audit of financial statements of the Condominium Management Authority for the year ended
31 December 2016 comprising the statement of financial position as at 31 December 2016 and
the statement of financial performance, statement of changes in equity and cash flow statement
for the year then ended and a summary of significant accounting policies and other explanatory
information, was Carried out under my direction in pursuance of provisions in Article 154(1) of
the Constitution of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka read in conjunction with
Section 13(1) of the Finance Act, No.38 of 1071 and Section 21 of the Common Amenities
Board Law, No.10 of 1073. My comments and observations which T consider should be
published with the Annual Report of the Authority in terms of Section 14(2)(c) of the Finance
Act appear in this report.

)         1.2 Management’s Responsibility for the Financial Statements

Management is responsible for the preparation and fair presentation of these financial
Statements in accordance with Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standards and for
Such internal control as the management determines is necessary to enable the preparation
of financial statements that are free from material misstatements whether due to fraud or

Crror.

1.3 Auditor’s Responsibility

My responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on my
audit. 1 conducted my audit in accordance with Sri Lanka Auditing Standards consistent

with International Auditing Standards of Supreme Audit Institutions (ISSAT 1000 —

ඈ 306/72, පාල ෆාර, බත්තරමුල්ල, ශී ලංකාට, .- මණ. 306/772, Gur gra! ai, LSI, Beis. No. 306/72. Polduwa Road, Batiaramulla, Sri Lanka

18310). Those Standards require that 1 comply with ethical requiremenis and plan and
perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements

are free from material misstatements.

An audit involves performing procedures to obtain audit evidence about the amounts and
disclosures in the financial statements. The procedures selected depend on the auditor's
judgement, including the assessment of the risks of material misstatement of the financial
statements, whether due to fraud or error. In making those risk assessments, the auditor
considers internal control relevant to the Authority’s preparation and fair presentation of
the financial statements in order to design audit procedures that are appropriate in the
circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of
the Authority’s internal control. An audit also includes evaluating the appropriateness of
accounting policies. used and the reasonableness  of accounting  estimates madc  by
management, as well as evaluating the overall presentation of financial statements. Sub-
sections (3) and (4) of Section 13 of the Finance Act, No.33 of 1071 give discretionary

powers to the Auditor General to determine the scope and extent of the audit.

I believe that the audit evidence I have obtained is sufficient an appropriate to provide a

basis for my audit opinion.

L4 Basis for Qualified Opinion

My opinion is qualified based on the matters described in paragraph 2.2 of this report.

1.        Financial Statements

2.1 Qualified Opinion

In my opinion, except for the effects of the matters described in paragraph 2.2 of this
report the financial statements give a true and fair view of the financial position of the
Condominium Management Authority as at 31 December 2016 and its financial
performance and cash flow for the year then ended in accordance with Sri Lanka Public

Sector Accounting Standards.

Comments on Financial Statements

Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standards

The following observations are made.

(a) Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 02

Adjustments made in the statement of changes in equity for the gratuity and
depreciations relating to the year 2015 amounting to Rs.650,410 and Rs.187,007
respectively had been adjusted to the cash flow for the operating activities in the cash
flow statement in the year under review .Nevertheless, the prior year adjustments
totalling Rs.1,130,822 made in the year under review had been adjusted to the cash

flow on the financial activities of the year under review.

(b) Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 07

As useful life time of an asset should be reviewed considering as a change of the
accounting estimate at the date of the end of the period reported in cach year.
Nevertheless, the Authority had not taken action in respect of the assets totalling
Rs.20.8° million had been fully depreciated but are being further used.

(©) SriLanka Public Sector Accounting Standard 0O

Even though, the final stock shall be computed and accounted at the lower value of
cost or net realizable value, contrary to that ,the Authority had valued the stock on
the cost without being computed at the net realizable valuc by making policy for the

stock .

2.2.2 Accounting Deficiencies

The following accounting deficiencies were observed.

(4) As the office rent which payments were completed in the year 2016 had been re-
allocated, the Office Rent Account and the Accrued Office Rent Account had

been over computed by Rs.115,802.

(b) Action had not been taken to pay or bring to account during the year under review
under current liabilities the gratuity amounting to Rs.315,418 which had been

allocated for an officer retired in the year 2016.

10

Financial Review

Financial Results

According to the financial statements presented, the surplus of the Authority for the year
ended 31 December 2016 amounted to Rs.70.41 million as compared with the
Corresponding surplus of Rs.21.97 million for the preceding year, thus indicating an
improvement of Rs.48.44 million in the financial results for the year under review as
compared with the preceding year. Even though receipt of Treasury provisions for the
payment of salaries had decreased by Rs.11 million as compared the year under review
with the preceding year, the increase of the operating income by a sum of Rs.76.8

million had been the main reason for the above improvement.

An analysis of the financial results of the year under review and the 04 preceding years
revealed that, despite the deficits incurred in the year 2013, surpluses had been earned in
other years . Even though the contribution of the Authority, after the adjustment of
employees’ remuneration, the taxes paid to the Government and the adjustment of
depreciation of non-current assets, had improved from the year 2012 to the year 2016, the
improvement in the year under review, as compared with the preceding year , was 53 per

Cent.

Analytical Financial Review

The following observations are made.

(a) Due to the income from the issue of certificates for the condominium properties
had increased by Rs.83.66 million or 107 per cent as compared with the preceding
year, the operating income of the year under review had been increased by
Rs.76.8 million or 72 per cent . As such, due to increase of the interest income for
fixed assets the non-operating income had been increased by Rs.6.16 million or

120 per cent as compared with the preceding year.

4.2        Management Activities

A sum of Rs.2.02 million had been paid in the year 1099 for a Private Company to
obtain 750 items out of the 02 category of goods necessary for the Authority and 545
items valued at Rs.1.22 million had been received in the year 2000. Action had not been
taken at the end of the year under review to settle the relevant money according to the
Judicial decree made in respect of the case filed by the Authority in the year 2006 as the

remaining goods had not been received.

4.3         Operating Review

v                      The following observations are made.

(4 Even though according to the Condominium Management Authority Act, No.10
of 1073 the Authority should have been maintained the Management Corporations
of the condominium properties actively, out of 872 Management Corporations
established by the Authority at the end of the year under review , 427 or 49 per

cent were inactive.

(b) Decision had been made to launch a book named “සහාධිපත්‍ය දේපළ වල සතුටින්‌ ගා
නිරෝගීව ජීවත්වීමේ රටාව * written by the Chairman of the Authority according to
the 108 decision of the Board of Management dated 25 May 2016 and the
printing expenditure of that book incurred by the fund of the Authority and
reimbursed . However, the Authority had printed a book in English medium
named “Condominium Living The Emerging Trend” incurrin a sum of Rs.l.07
million .The royalty of this book had owned to the Chairman and the Authority

had failed to settle the printing expenditure as at the end of the year under review.

4.4 Utilization of Funds

Even though a sum of Rs.80 million had been received from the Treasury in the years
2015 and 2016 for the modernization of the infrastructure of 03 Flats under “Nagamu
Puravara”Project, a sum of Rs.32.7 million had been returned to the Ministry without

being utilized in any activity due to failure to fulfill the expected objectives properly.

4.5       Identified Losses

The Authority had not included the Cost of Living Allowance in the calculation of the
Employce Provident Fund and Employee Trust Fund for the period from January 2000 to
December 2013 contrary to Section 47 of the Employee Provident Fund Act.No.l5 of
1058. As such, action had not been taken to recovery of the sum of Rs.4.47 milion which
was the employee share included in the outstanding Employee Provident Fund
amounting to Rs.11.18 million paid by the Authority from the relevant persons . Further
the Authority had to pay a surcharge of Rs.6.36 million for that outstanding money and a
sum of Rs.2.94 million had been paid for that purpose in the year 2010.

Accountability and Good Governance

Action Plan

The following observations are made

(a) Annual Procurement Plan, Human Resources Development Plan and Internal
Audit Plan should be included in the Action Plan in terms of the Paragraph 5-2 of
the Public Finance Circular No.01/2014 dated 17 February 2014. However, those

had not been included init.

(bh Even though plans had been made to complete the amendments of the
Condominium Property Management Authority Act, No.10 of 1073 in August
2015 , according to the Action Plan of the year 2016 that period had been
extended up to February 2016. However, that activities had not been completed
by the end of the year under review and the relevant Act had been referred to the

Department of Legal Draftsman.

Budgetary Control

According to the financial statements presented by the Authority, actual income and
expenditure revealed variances ranging from 15 per cent to 87 per cent, thus indicating
that the budget had not been made use of as an effective instrument of financial

management control.

Tabling of Annual Reports

The Authority had not tabled the Annual Reports relevant to the years 2013,2014 and

2015 in parliament even at the end of the year under review.

Financial Statement

NOTES TO ACCOUNTS

1. Notes to accounts

These accounting statements have been presented in compliance with generally accepted accounting principles and
by selecting the Sri Lanka public sector accounting policies endorsed by the public sector accounting standards com-
mittee, preparing accounting estimates in timely and fair manner.

It is assured that measures have been taken to present fair financial statements by designing implementing and main-
taining internal control relevant to the preparation and fair presentation of financial statements that are free from
material misstatement, whether due to fraud or error.

2. Accounting Policies

The accounting reports of the Authority have been presented with mutual interconnection between periods of time
and on historic cost basis in accordance with recognized accounting policies. Adjustments have been made towards
inflationary factors that may affect the financial policies and the accounting reports have been prepared on accrual
basis.

3. Location of the Authority

The Condominium Management Authority is located at the National Housing Development Authority at Sir Chittam-
palam A Gardianer Mawatha, Colombo 02 and carries out regulatory duties in respect of condominium properties
Covering the entire island.

4. Legal nature of the Authority

In terms of the powers conferred under the Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No. 24 of 2003, itis the
responsibility of the Authority to establish management corporations for the maintenance administration and control
of common elements and common amenities in condominium properties and to ensure that common facilities are
provided so as to fulfill the needs of stakeholders.

5. Legislation relevant for the administration of operations of the Authority
e Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Law No.l0 of 1073
° Common Amenities Board Act No. 46 of 1082
e Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No 24 of 2003
e Apartment Ownership Act No. 11 of 1073
e Apartment Ownership (Amendment) Act No. 45 of 1982
e Apartment Ownership {Special Provisions) No.04 19000
e Apartment Ownership (Amendment) Act 39 of 2003
6. Fixed assets

The provisions for depreciation for fixed assets are calculated by using straight line basis from the date of purchase to
the date of sale as per the policy of the Authority

e      Motor vehicles                                  -25% on Cost
e      Office furniture                                 -20% on cost
e      Machinery and equipment                 - 20% on cost
e      Office equipment                              - 20% on cost
e      Buildings                                       - 04% on cost

7. Gratuity

Allocations have been made in accounts for the value of the gratuity to be paid for all employees who serve ineh
Authority. The value of such allocations relevant to the year ended 31st December 2016 was Rs. 31,791,603 and of
that amount Rs 30,305, 186.00 had been invested as shown below as at 31.12.2016.

8. Stocks

Purchasing of stocks are valued at cost and adjusted in accounts and no profit percentage has been included init.
9. Revenue

Profit/loss accounts have been prepared on the basis of gross revenue.

10. Allocations for bad and doubtful debt

Allocations for bad and doubtful debt have been made on outcome on the basis of the age analysis of the debtors
existing as at the end of the year.

e      Years 0-2         10% 1,485,175
Ul)      Years 2-3         20% 42,980

e      Years 3-4         30% 2,101,150
e      Years 4-5          50% 206,416

Ul)      Over 5 years     100% 3,049,403
Accordingly, a sum of Rs. 6,975,133 has been allocated in the accounts of the current year for bad and doubtful debt.

11. Acase has been filed in the district court of Colombo under case number 53429/MR to recover Rs 807,187 due
from Lanka Net (Pvt) Ltd. As there no contingent liabilities in respect of cases filed by or against the Authority, no
allocations have been made in the accounts for that purpose.

12. Alease lend of Rs. 17,912,410 on 5 year repayment basis has been obtained from Bank of Ceylon for 03 Cars and
01 cab purchased in the year 2012 and according to the accounts, a sum of Rs. 1,689,850 remains to be paid for the
said lease lend.

13. EPF and ETF in arrears

As per the provisions of the Act, the cost of living allowance has not been taken into account in paying contributions
of the employees of the Authority for the Employees Provident Fund and the Employees’ Trust Fund from January
2006 to December 2013.

Accordingly, action has been taken to allocate Rs. 18,705,203 in the accounts for the settlement of said arrears and
as at 31.12.2016, Rs. 15,646,908 of that amount remains to paid to the EPF and ETF. The Department of Labour has
granted a grace period of one year for the payment of that amount. Action has been taken to set aside provisions
amounting to Rs. 3,058,294 in the accounts payable as at 31.12.2016.

14. Capital projects

Under the provisions allocated in the year 2015 for capital projects, Rs. 30,000,000 and Rs. 151,616,106 were allo-
cated for the current year and those amounts the emergency repairs of housing schemes constructed by the gov-
ernment. Of the said provisions Rs 76,747,310 was used for the renovation of housing schemes and rehabilitation of
road network of three housing schemes and since Rs. 32,659,485 out of Rs.80,000,000 granted for the renovation
of housing schemes remained unspent, action has been taken to make provisions in the accounts to release that

ol

amount back the Ministry. Further, action has been taken to set aside Rs 42,209,931for the remaining work of the
project for the restoration of roads in 03 housing schemes and the project for the grant of title deeds to residents of
Tsunami housing schemes.

15. Bonus shares

In pursuance of approval referred to by Ministry of Public Administration, Housing and Construction dat-
ed 12.01.1084, 5000 shares of Rs 100 were obtained from the Housing Development Finance Corporation on
19.01.1084.

A bonus share issue of 25,000 shares in respect of the value of the said shares was issued on 29.06.2000. Accordingly,
action has been taken to disclose in the accounts an investment of Rs. 3,000,000 for 30,000 shares of Rs. 100 each of
the HDFC in possession of this Authority.

16. Income Tax

Provisions have been allocated in accounts for the payment of Rs. 19,347,062 as income tax on the basis of the profit
of Rs. 89,757,941 for the said year as at 31.12.2016.

17. Previous year adjustments

Action has been taken to credit Rs 277,618 to the previous year adjustment account as the corrections in respect of
previous year and to debit a sum of Rs.1,408,440 to the previous year adjustment account.

18. Accounting government grants

In the year 2015 too, the Treasury had allocated Rs. 80,000,000 for the renovation activities of three housing
schemes under the ‘Nagamu Puravara’ project and out of that amount Rs. 30,000,000 was granted during the current
year.

19. Allocation for depreciation

Action has been taken for depreciation on the basis of percentages indicated in Note 06 under fixed assets. Accord-
ingly, action was taken to adjust Rs. 4,069,969 to the profit of the current year as the value of annual depreciation.

Similarly, owing to the deductions of Rs 88,981 from the annual depreciation for machinery and equipment and Rs
98,026 from the annual depreciation value for office furniture and accessories onn account of the previous year ad-
justments, the value of depreciation allocation for the year is shown as Rs 3,882,063 under Note 01.
